AI Analysis

TL;DR: WPC T-GM grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock (class 248), collapsing all 4 suites; pmc argument bug added 5 independent failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all BC/slave/follower sync tests

Affects: tgm (5/5), dualnicbcha (~6/8), dualnicbc (~6/9), dualfollower (3/3). The WPC T-GM node hosting linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never transitioned out of FREERUN during the run. With no locked GM advertising Announce messages, the entire downstream chain — BC → dualnicbc → dualnicbcha → dualfollower slaves — could not lock. The tgm log stream stayed open but hit context deadline exceeded after 340 s without ever emitting a LOCKED event; all four state-based tgm tests timed out on Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM / : false. The dualfollower node cnfdf31 exhibits both missing openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3 stuck in LISTENING — consistent with no upstream Announce to trigger SLAVE election.


• 5/25 failures — pmc invoked with split arguments; GET PARENT_DATA_SET rejected as two bad commands

Affects: dualnicbc ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and dualnicbcha ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master"). pmc is called with GET and PARENT_DATA_SET as separate argv elements; the binary responds bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. Identical verbatim error appears in both suites, ruling out a flake. Likely triggered by the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary (linuxptp ≥ 4.3, el10_2) changing batch-mode argument tokenization, or the test helper failing to quote the combined string. Other pmc queries (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET) still succeed, confirming the socket and ptp4l process are reachable.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN / GNSS never lockedAll 3~6~6All 5
pmc split-arg bug—32—

• The GM FREERUN failure is shared across all 4 suites — it is the single largest driver and the only failure in tgm and dualfollower.
• The pmc split-arg bug is shared between dualnicbc and dualnicbcha only (suites that exercise PARENT_DATA_SET queries via the BC node).
• No failures are genuinely suite-specific; the dualfollower and tgm failures are pure downstream consequences of the shared GM not locking.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job and inspect GM GNSS hardware first. Confirm whether the WPC T-GM node achieves GNSS/DPLL lock in a fresh run. If it fails again, check the GNSS antenna cable, receiver status, and ts2phc DPLL netlink events on that node. This single fix would resolve ~20/25 failures.

2. Fix pmc invocation to pass GET PARENT_DATA_SET as a single quoted argument. In both the test helper (ptp-operator-conformance-test) and any exec.Command / shell call in linuxptp-daemon, ensure the action+management-ID are passed as one argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET")), or switch to the interactive RunPMCExpGetParentDS path with lowercase command ("get PARENT_DATA_SET") to match the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary's expected input. This resolves the remaining 5 failures.

3. Add a pre-flight GM-lock gate to the CI job. Before running any BC/slave/follower suite, assert that the T-GM node has clock class ≤ 7 (LOCKED); fail fast with a clear infra error rather than letting all 4 suites time out. This would surface the GNSS issue immediately and save ~30 min of wasted CI time per run.


Overall Issue Class: test_flake (dominant: GNSS hardware failure is a known lab environmental flake) + test_regression (secondary: pmc argument bug introduced with RHCOS 10.2 / linuxptp upstream sync 0459bc0)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — 25/25 failures, 4/4 suites completely down in a nightly periodic job.




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out waiting for node cnfdf31's follower interfaces to reach LOCKED state because the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never emitted by linuxptp-daemon, and ens2f3np3 was stuck in LISTENING rather than SLAVE role.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Slave node never locked — missing clock_state metric and port stuck in LISTENING (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Tests 1 & 2 — identical error

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test",

slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found,

available op[tions: ...]

```

```

Test 3 — additional symptom

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig temp

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="",

slaveIfs=[ens2f3np3 ens2f0np0]). Per-interface results:

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found

```

```

Broader context from other suites (junit-failures.txt)

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

```

tgm suite (junit-failures.txt)

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6)

...clock class: 248 (← default/FREERUN value, never reached 6)

```

• Root Cause: The openshift_ptp_clock_state metric (registered in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/metrics/register.go:57-63 with labels {process, node, iface}) is only set when UpdateClockStateMetrics() in pkg/metrics/exporter.go:15-23 is called with a servo state change for that interface. A metric label combination {node=cnfdf31, iface=ens2f0np0} being entirely absent means linuxptp-daemon on cnfdf31 never processed a servo state log line for ens2f0np0 — i.e., ptp4l never elected that port as SLAVE and never emitted a servo lock event. The explicit role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) in Test 3 for ens2f3np3 corroborates this: both follower ports are stuck in LISTENING/unelected state. The tgm suite failures (clock class 248 = freerun, never 6) indicate the upstream Grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock; with the T-GM in freerun the entire downstream chain — BC → dualfollower slave — cannot lock, which is consistent with all suites failing in the same run. Additionally, the pmc bad command: GET / PARENT_DATA_SET errors in the dualnicbc suite (same run, linuxptp-daemon branch release-5.0) indicate a ptp4l management interface issue. The commit OCPBUGS-90708: Sync from upstream (22-Jun-2026) in linuxptp-daemon (merged 2026-06-23, two days after this run) and the commit OCPBUGS-88369: Fix CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs in cloud-event-proxy (merged 2026-06-25) were both pending at the time of this job.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely pre-dates the fix in linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (OCPBUGS-90708 / CNF-24996, merged 2026-06-23, SHA 0459bc0) and cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (OCPBUGS-88369, merged 2026-06-25, SHA fc5d567) — both merged after this CI run on 2026-06-21. The breaking change introducing the regression is Unknown (upstream/downstream commit not visible in the shallow clone).
• Is it a flake? No — all four test suites in the same job (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) failed with consistent, correlated errors. The T-GM staying at clock class 248 is a systematic failure, not random jitter.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the T-GM node achieves GNSS lock (clock class 6) before running downstream sync tests; also ensure the linuxptp-daemon and cloud-event-proxy images built from release-5.0 include the fixes from OCPBUGS-90708 (pmc/ptp4l management interface fix) and OCPBUGS-88369 (CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs), both of which were merged after this job ran.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 9 failures stem from two independent root causes: pmc being invoked with split arguments causing PARENT_DATA_SET queries to return "bad command" errors, and the BC node's ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) due to an unlocked upstream GM — with event-framework consumer timeouts as a downstream consequence.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: PMC "bad command" for PARENT_DATA_SET (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: The pmc tool is being invoked with "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as two separate argv elements rather than as the single combined string "GET PARENT_DATA_SET". In non-interactive (batch) mode, linuxptp's pmc.c calls do_command(argv[optind]) for each remaining argv item; processing "GET" alone yields "bad command: GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone yields "bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET". Other pmc commands (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET used by the clock-class test) still work, confirming ptp4l itself is up and the socket is reachable — only the argument quoting for PARENT_DATA_SET queries is broken. The new non-interactive helper RunPMCGetParentDS in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 passes the full "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string as one exec.Command arg (which should be fine via sscanf tokenizing). The split-arg pattern strongly implicates the test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test calling pmc ... GET PARENT_DATA_SET without quoting, or a behavior change in the RHEL 10 linuxptp pmc binary that now treats the space-separated arg as two tokens.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0 — "upstream-sync-2026-06-22", merged 2026-06-22) which synced upstream linuxptp changes into release-5.0; the pmc binary on RHEL 10 / RHCOS 10.2 may have changed its batch-mode argument-parsing behaviour. Test code path: /tmp/cnf-C4K0w/ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (not cloned, exact commit unknown).
• Is it a flake? No — identical error appears verbatim across dualnicbc AND dualnicbcha suites in the same run, showing systematic breakage.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure pmc is invoked with the action and management-ID as a single quoted argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configPath, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") in Go, or pmc ... "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" in shell). Alternatively, switch all GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to the interactive expect-based RunPMCExpGetParentDS (linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:132) which uses e.Send("GET PARENT_DATA_SET\n") and is known to work.

• Group 2: BC ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "PTP metric is present verifies on slave", "The slave node network interface is taken down and up", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published ... cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString>: incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Cross-corroborating evidence from tgm suite (same CI run):

```

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6) ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM, Expected : false to be true

```

• Root Cause: The WPC Grandmaster node (tgm) itself is not reaching LOCKED state (clock class 6) — demonstrated by multiple tgm suite failures in the same CI run reporting clock class never reaches 6. With the GM in FREERUN/HOLDOVER (class 248), the BC node (cnfdf32, running ptpconfig test-bc-master1 against ptp4l.1.config) cannot lock its upstream port ens2f0np0, causing ptp4l to report class 248. After the network-outage test brings ens2f0np0 down and up, ptp4l without a valid upstream GM elects itself MASTER on that port instead of returning to SLAVE. PTP time-sync metrics (openshift_ptp_clock_state, openshift_ptp_offset_ns) are absent because the linuxptp-daemon does not emit offset/clock-state metrics when not locked; CNE event metrics (cne_api_events_published) are present showing cloud-event-proxy is running but the PTP layer is FREERUN.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — tgm (WPC GNSS/GM hardware) failures point to either a hardware/environment issue on the telco5g lab testbed or a change in the GM node's configuration/firmware. The linuxptp-daemon upstream sync PR #613 (0459bc0, 2026-06-22) is a candidate if it changed ts2phc or WPC GM handling.
• Is it a flake? No — 4 separate tests in dualnicbc plus parallel tests and matching tgm failures all confirm systemic FREERUN state.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate and restore the WPC GM node's GNSS/GPS signal lock (tgm hardware/config), or check whether PR #613's upstream sync changed ts2phc GM behaviour. Once the GM reaches class 6, all BC and slave downstream clock-class/metric/outage-recovery tests should pass.

• Group 3: Cloud-event-proxy PushInitialValue timeout (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "PTP Slave Clock Sync" [parallel])
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The consumer pod in ptp-event-framework-test never logs "Got CurrentState: ({.*})", meaning it does not receive an initial state push from the cloud-event-proxy sidecar after the linuxptp-daemon pod restart. The most recent cloud-event-proxy commit is fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime" (PR #701). If this PR changed how dual-NIC BC events are published (e.g., restructuring which publisher emits SyncStateChange for TBC profiles — see cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:388-393), the initial-state push path PushInitialValue may no longer fire on daemon restart for this BC topology. An alternative explanation is that with ptp4l in FREERUN (Group 2), no LOCKED→FREERUN state transition occurs at restart, so no event is generated to push.
• Breaking PR/Commit: cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime"), merged just before this CI run. Reference: cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:375-393 and metrics/tbc_test.go.
• Is it a flake? No — same timeou

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published ... cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString>: incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Cross-corroborating evidence from tgm suite (same CI run):

```

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6) ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM, Expected : false to be true

```

• Root Cause: The WPC Grandmaster node (tgm) itself is not reaching LOCKED state (clock class 6) — demonstrated by multiple tgm suite failures in the same CI run reporting clock class never reaches 6. With the GM in FREERUN/HOLDOVER (class 248), the BC node (cnfdf32, running ptpconfig test-bc-master1 against ptp4l.1.config) cannot lock its upstream port ens2f0np0, causing ptp4l to report class 248. After the network-outage test brings ens2f0np0 down and up, ptp4l without a valid upstream GM elects itself MASTER on that port instead of returning to SLAVE. PTP time-sync metrics (openshift_ptp_clock_state, openshift_ptp_offset_ns) are absent because the linuxptp-daemon does not emit offset/clock-state metrics when not locked; CNE event metrics (cne_api_events_published) are present showing cloud-event-proxy is running but the PTP layer is FREERUN.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — tgm (WPC GNSS/GM hardware) failures point to either a hardware/environment issue on the telco5g lab testbed or a change in the GM node's configuration/firmware. The linuxptp-daemon upstream sync PR #613 (0459bc0, 2026-06-22) is a candidate if it changed ts2phc or WPC GM handling.
• Is it a flake? No — 4 separate tests in dualnicbc plus parallel tests and matching tgm failures all confirm systemic FREERUN state.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate and restore the WPC GM node's GNSS/GPS signal lock (tgm hardware/config), or check whether PR #613's upstream sync changed ts2phc GM behaviour. Once the GM reaches class 6, all BC and slave downstream clock-class/metric/outage-recovery tests should pass.

• Group 3: Cloud-event-proxy PushInitialValue timeout (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "PTP Slave Clock Sync" [parallel])
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The consumer pod in ptp-event-framework-test never logs "Got CurrentState: ({.*})", meaning it does not receive an initial state push from the cloud-event-proxy sidecar after the linuxptp-daemon pod restart. The most recent cloud-event-proxy commit is fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime" (PR #701). If this PR changed how dual-NIC BC events are published (e.g., restructuring which publisher emits SyncStateChange for TBC profiles — see cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:388-393), the initial-state push path PushInitialValue may no longer fire on daemon restart for this BC topology. An alternative explanation is that with ptp4l in FREERUN (Group 2), no LOCKED→FREERUN state transition occurs at restart, so no event is generated to push.
• Breaking PR/Commit: cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime"), merged just before this CI run. Reference: cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:375-393 and metrics/tbc_test.go.
• Is it a flake? No — same timeou


TL;DR: WPC T-GM grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock (class 248), collapsing all 4 suites; pmc argument bug added 5 independent failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all BC/slave/follower sync tests

Affects: tgm (5/5), dualnicbcha (~6/8), dualnicbc (~6/9), dualfollower (3/3). The WPC T-GM node hosting linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never transitioned out of FREERUN during the run. With no locked GM advertising Announce messages, the entire downstream chain — BC → dualnicbc → dualnicbcha → dualfollower slaves — could not lock. The tgm log stream stayed open but hit context deadline exceeded after 340 s without ever emitting a LOCKED event; all four state-based tgm tests timed out on Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM / : false. The dualfollower node cnfdf31 exhibits both missing openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3 stuck in LISTENING — consistent with no upstream Announce to trigger SLAVE election.


• 5/25 failures — pmc invoked with split arguments; GET PARENT_DATA_SET rejected as two bad commands

Affects: dualnicbc ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and dualnicbcha ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master"). pmc is called with GET and PARENT_DATA_SET as separate argv elements; the binary responds bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. Identical verbatim error appears in both suites, ruling out a flake. Likely triggered by the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary (linuxptp ≥ 4.3, el10_2) changing batch-mode argument tokenization, or the test helper failing to quote the combined string. Other pmc queries (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET) still succeed, confirming the socket and ptp4l process are reachable.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN / GNSS never lockedAll 3~6~6All 5
pmc split-arg bug—32—

• The GM FREERUN failure is shared across all 4 suites — it is the single largest driver and the only failure in tgm and dualfollower.
• The pmc split-arg bug is shared between dualnicbc and dualnicbcha only (suites that exercise PARENT_DATA_SET queries via the BC node).
• No failures are genuinely suite-specific; the dualfollower and tgm failures are pure downstream consequences of the shared GM not locking.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job and inspect GM GNSS hardware first. Confirm whether the WPC T-GM node achieves GNSS/DPLL lock in a fresh run. If it fails again, check the GNSS antenna cable, receiver status, and ts2phc DPLL netlink events on that node. This single fix would resolve ~20/25 failures.

2. Fix pmc invocation to pass GET PARENT_DATA_SET as a single quoted argument. In both the test helper (ptp-operator-conformance-test) and any exec.Command / shell call in linuxptp-daemon, ensure the action+management-ID are passed as one argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET")), or switch to the interactive RunPMCExpGetParentDS path with lowercase command ("get PARENT_DATA_SET") to match the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary's expected input. This resolves the remaining 5 failures.

3. Add a pre-flight GM-lock gate to the CI job. Before running any BC/slave/follower suite, assert that the T-GM node has clock class ≤ 7 (LOCKED); fail fast with a clear infra error rather than letting all 4 suites time out. This would surface the GNSS issue immediately and save ~30 min of wasted CI time per run.


Overall Issue Class: test_flake (dominant: GNSS hardware failure is a known lab environmental flake) + test_regression (secondary: pmc argument bug introduced with RHCOS 10.2 / linuxptp upstream sync 0459bc0)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — 25/25 failures, 4/4 suites completely down in a nightly periodic job.




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out waiting for node cnfdf31's follower interfaces to reach LOCKED state because the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never emitted by linuxptp-daemon, and ens2f3np3 was stuck in LISTENING rather than SLAVE role.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Slave node never locked — missing clock_state metric and port stuck in LISTENING (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Tests 1 & 2 — identical error

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test",

slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found,

available op[tions: ...]

```

```

Test 3 — additional symptom

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig temp

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="",

slaveIfs=[ens2f3np3 ens2f0np0]). Per-interface results:

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found

```

```

Broader context from other suites (junit-failures.txt)

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

```

tgm suite (junit-failures.txt)

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6)

...clock class: 248 (← default/FREERUN value, never reached 6)

```

• Root Cause: The openshift_ptp_clock_state metric (registered in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/metrics/register.go:57-63 with labels {process, node, iface}) is only set when UpdateClockStateMetrics() in pkg/metrics/exporter.go:15-23 is called with a servo state change for that interface. A metric label combination {node=cnfdf31, iface=ens2f0np0} being entirely absent means linuxptp-daemon on cnfdf31 never processed a servo state log line for ens2f0np0 — i.e., ptp4l never elected that port as SLAVE and never emitted a servo lock event. The explicit role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) in Test 3 for ens2f3np3 corroborates this: both follower ports are stuck in LISTENING/unelected state. The tgm suite failures (clock class 248 = freerun, never 6) indicate the upstream Grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock; with the T-GM in freerun the entire downstream chain — BC → dualfollower slave — cannot lock, which is consistent with all suites failing in the same run. Additionally, the pmc bad command: GET / PARENT_DATA_SET errors in the dualnicbc suite (same run, linuxptp-daemon branch release-5.0) indicate a ptp4l management interface issue. The commit OCPBUGS-90708: Sync from upstream (22-Jun-2026) in linuxptp-daemon (merged 2026-06-23, two days after this run) and the commit OCPBUGS-88369: Fix CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs in cloud-event-proxy (merged 2026-06-25) were both pending at the time of this job.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely pre-dates the fix in linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (OCPBUGS-90708 / CNF-24996, merged 2026-06-23, SHA 0459bc0) and cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (OCPBUGS-88369, merged 2026-06-25, SHA fc5d567) — both merged after this CI run on 2026-06-21. The breaking change introducing the regression is Unknown (upstream/downstream commit not visible in the shallow clone).
• Is it a flake? No — all four test suites in the same job (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) failed with consistent, correlated errors. The T-GM staying at clock class 248 is a systematic failure, not random jitter.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the T-GM node achieves GNSS lock (clock class 6) before running downstream sync tests; also ensure the linuxptp-daemon and cloud-event-proxy images built from release-5.0 include the fixes from OCPBUGS-90708 (pmc/ptp4l management interface fix) and OCPBUGS-88369 (CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs), both of which were merged after this job ran.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 9 failures stem from two independent root causes: pmc being invoked with split arguments causing PARENT_DATA_SET queries to return "bad command" errors, and the BC node's ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) due to an unlocked upstream GM — with event-framework consumer timeouts as a downstream consequence.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: PMC "bad command" for PARENT_DATA_SET (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: The pmc tool is being invoked with "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as two separate argv elements rather than as the single combined string "GET PARENT_DATA_SET". In non-interactive (batch) mode, linuxptp's pmc.c calls do_command(argv[optind]) for each remaining argv item; processing "GET" alone yields "bad command: GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone yields "bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET". Other pmc commands (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET used by the clock-class test) still work, confirming ptp4l itself is up and the socket is reachable — only the argument quoting for PARENT_DATA_SET queries is broken. The new non-interactive helper RunPMCGetParentDS in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 passes the full "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string as one exec.Command arg (which should be fine via sscanf tokenizing). The split-arg pattern strongly implicates the test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test calling pmc ... GET PARENT_DATA_SET without quoting, or a behavior change in the RHEL 10 linuxptp pmc binary that now treats the space-separated arg as two tokens.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0 — "upstream-sync-2026-06-22", merged 2026-06-22) which synced upstream linuxptp changes into release-5.0; the pmc binary on RHEL 10 / RHCOS 10.2 may have changed its batch-mode argument-parsing behaviour. Test code path: /tmp/cnf-C4K0w/ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (not cloned, exact commit unknown).
• Is it a flake? No — identical error appears verbatim across dualnicbc AND dualnicbcha suites in the same run, showing systematic breakage.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure pmc is invoked with the action and management-ID as a single quoted argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configPath, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") in Go, or pmc ... "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" in shell). Alternatively, switch all GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to the interactive expect-based RunPMCExpGetParentDS (linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:132) which uses e.Send("GET PARENT_DATA_SET\n") and is known to work.

• Group 2: BC ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "PTP metric is present verifies on slave", "The slave node network interface is taken down and up", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published ... cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString>: incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Cross-corroborating evidence from tgm suite (same CI run):

```

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6) ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM, Expected : false to be true

```

• Root Cause: The WPC Grandmaster node (tgm) itself is not reaching LOCKED state (clock class 6) — demonstrated by multiple tgm suite failures in the same CI run reporting clock class never reaches 6. After the network-outage test brings ens2f0np0 down and up, ptp4l without a valid upstream GM elects itself MASTER on that port instead of returning to SLAVE. PTP time-sync metrics (openshift_ptp_clock_state, openshift_ptp_offset_ns) are absent because the linuxptp-daemon does not emit offset/clock-state metrics when not locked; CNE event metrics (cne_api_events_published) are present showing cloud-event-proxy is running but the PTP layer is FREERUN.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — tgm (WPC GNSS/GM hardware) failures point to either a hardware/environment issue on the telco5g lab testbed or a change in the GM node's configuration/firmware. The linuxptp-daemon upstream sync PR #613 (0459bc0, 2026-06-22) is a candidate if it changed ts2phc or WPC GM handling.
• Is it a flake? No — 4 separate tests in dualnicbc plus parallel tests and matching tgm failures all confirm systemic FREERUN state.

dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 9 failures stem from two independent root causes: pmc being invoked with split arguments causing PARENT_DATA_SET queries to return "bad command" errors, and the BC node's ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) due to an unlocked upstream GM — with event-framework consumer timeouts as a downstream consequence.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: PMC "bad command" for PARENT_DATA_SET (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: The pmc tool is being invoked with "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as two separate argv elements rather than as the single combined string "GET PARENT_DATA_SET". In non-interactive (batch) mode, linuxptp's pmc.c calls do_command(argv[optind]) for each remaining argv item; processing "GET" alone yields "bad command: GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone yields "bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET". Other pmc commands (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET used by the clock-class test) still work, confirming ptp4l itself is up and the socket is reachable — only the argument quoting for PARENT_DATA_SET queries is broken. The new non-interactive helper RunPMCGetParentDS in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 passes the full "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string as one exec.Command arg (which should be fine via sscanf tokenizing). The split-arg pattern strongly implicates the test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test calling pmc ... GET PARENT_DATA_SET without quoting, or a behavior change in the RHEL 10 linuxptp pmc binary that now treats the space-separated arg as two tokens.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0 — "upstream-sync-2026-06-22", merged 2026-06-22) which synced upstream linuxptp changes into release-5.0; the pmc binary on RHEL 10 / RHCOS 10.2 may have changed its batch-mode argument-parsing behaviour. Test code path: /tmp/cnf-C4K0w/ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (not cloned, exact commit unknown).
• Is it a flake? No — identical error appears verbatim across dualnicbc AND dualnicbcha suites in the same run, showing systematic breakage.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure pmc is invoked with the action and management-ID as a single quoted argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configPath, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") in Go, or pmc ... "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" in shell). Alternatively, switch all GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to the interactive expect-based RunPMCExpGetParentDS (linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:132) which uses e.Send("GET PARENT_DATA_SET\n") and is known to work.

• Group 2: BC ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "PTP metric is present verifies on slave", "The slave node network interface is taken down and up", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published ... cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString>: incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Cross-corroborating evidence from tgm suite (same CI run):

```

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6) ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM, Expected : false to be true

```

• Root Cause: The WPC Grandmaster node (tgm) itself is not reaching LOCKED state (clock class 6) — demonstrated by multiple tgm suite failures in the same CI run reporting clock class never reaches 6. With the GM in FREERUN/HOLDOVER (class 248), the BC node (cnfdf32, running ptpconfig test-bc-master1 against ptp4l.1.config) cannot lock its upstream port ens2f0np0, causing ptp4l to report class 248. After the network-outage test brings ens2f0np0 down and up, ptp4l without a valid upstream GM elects itself MASTER on that port instead of returning to SLAVE. PTP time-sync metrics (openshift_ptp_clock_state, openshift_ptp_offset_ns) are absent because the linuxptp-daemon does not emit offset/clock-state metrics when not locked; CNE event metrics (cne_api_events_published) are present showing cloud-event-proxy is running but the PTP layer is FREERUN.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — tgm (WPC GNSS/GM hardware) failures point to either a hardware/environment issue on the telco5g lab testbed or a change in the GM node's configuration/firmware. The linuxptp-daemon upstream sync PR #613 (0459bc0, 2026-06-22) is a candidate if it changed ts2phc or WPC GM handling.
• Is it a flake? No — 4 separate tests in dualnicbc plus parallel tests and matching tgm failures all confirm systemic FREERUN state.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate and restore the WPC GM node's GNSS/GPS signal lock (tgm hardware/config), or check whether PR #613's upstream sync changed ts2phc GM behaviour. Once the GM reaches class 6, all BC and slave downstream clock-class/metric/outage-recovery tests should pass.

• Group 3: Cloud-event-proxy PushInitialValue timeout (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "PTP Slave Clock Sync" [parallel])
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The consumer pod in ptp-event-framework-test never logs "Got CurrentState: ({.*})", meaning it does not receive an initial state push from the cloud-event-proxy sidecar after the linuxptp-daemon pod restart. The most recent cloud-event-proxy commit is fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime" (PR #701). If this PR changed how dual-NIC BC events are published (e.g., restructuring which publisher emits SyncStateChange for TBC profiles — see cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:388-393), the initial-state push path PushInitialValue may no longer fire on daemon restart for this BC topology. An alternative explanation is that with ptp4l in FREERUN (Group 2), no LOCKED→FREERUN state transition occurs at restart, so no event is generated to push.
• Breaking PR/Commit: cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime"), merged just before this CI run. Reference: cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:375-393 and metrics/tbc_test.go.
• Is it a flake? No — same timeou


TL;DR: WPC T-GM grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock (class 248), collapsing all 4 suites; pmc argument bug added 5 independent failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all BC/slave/follower sync tests

Affects: tgm (5/5), dualnicbcha (~6/8), dualnicbc (~6/9), dualfollower (3/3). The WPC T-GM node hosting linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never transitioned out of FREERUN during the run. With no locked GM advertising Announce messages, the entire downstream chain — BC → dualnicbc → dualnicbcha → dualfollower slaves — could not lock. The tgm log stream stayed open but hit context deadline exceeded after 340 s without ever emitting a LOCKED event; all four state-based tgm tests timed out on Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM / : false. The dualfollower node cnfdf31 exhibits both missing openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3 stuck in LISTENING — consistent with no upstream Announce to trigger SLAVE election.


• 5/25 failures — pmc invoked with split arguments; GET PARENT_DATA_SET rejected as two bad commands

Affects: dualnicbc ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and dualnicbcha ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master"). pmc is called with GET and PARENT_DATA_SET as separate argv elements; the binary responds bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. Identical verbatim error appears in both suites, ruling out a flake. Likely triggered by the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary (linuxptp ≥ 4.3, el10_2) changing batch-mode argument tokenization, or the test helper failing to quote the combined string. Other pmc queries (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET) still succeed, confirming the socket and ptp4l process are reachable.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN / GNSS never lockedAll 3~6~6All 5
pmc split-arg bug—32—

• The GM FREERUN failure is shared across all 4 suites — it is the single largest driver and the only failure in tgm and dualfollower.
• The pmc split-arg bug is shared between dualnicbc and dualnicbcha only (suites that exercise PARENT_DATA_SET queries via the BC node).
• No failures are genuinely suite-specific; the dualfollower and tgm failures are pure downstream consequences of the shared GM not locking.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job and inspect GM GNSS hardware first. Confirm whether the WPC T-GM node achieves GNSS/DPLL lock in a fresh run. If it fails again, check the GNSS antenna cable, receiver status, and ts2phc DPLL netlink events on that node. This single fix would resolve ~20/25 failures.

2. Fix pmc invocation to pass GET PARENT_DATA_SET as a single quoted argument. In both the test helper (ptp-operator-conformance-test) and any exec.Command / shell call in linuxptp-daemon, ensure the action+management-ID are passed as one argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET")), or switch to the interactive RunPMCExpGetParentDS path with lowercase command ("get PARENT_DATA_SET") to match the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary's expected input. This resolves the remaining 5 failures.

3. Add a pre-flight GM-lock gate to the CI job. Before running any BC/slave/follower suite, assert that the T-GM node has clock class ≤ 7 (LOCKED); fail fast with a clear infra error rather than letting all 4 suites time out. This would surface the GNSS issue immediately and save ~30 min of wasted CI time per run.


Overall Issue Class: test_flake (dominant: GNSS hardware failure is a known lab environmental flake) + test_regression (secondary: pmc argument bug introduced with RHCOS 10.2 / linuxptp upstream sync 0459bc0)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — 25/25 failures, 4/4 suites completely down in a nightly periodic job.




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out waiting for node cnfdf31's follower interfaces to reach LOCKED state because the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never emitted by linuxptp-daemon, and ens2f3np3 was stuck in LISTENING rather than SLAVE role.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Slave node never locked — missing clock_state metric and port stuck in LISTENING (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Tests 1 & 2 — identical error

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test",

slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found,

available op[tions: ...]

```

```

Test 3 — additional symptom

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig temp

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="",

slaveIfs=[ens2f3np3 ens2f0np0]). Per-interface results:

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found

```

```

Broader context from other suites (junit-failures.txt)

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

```

tgm suite (junit-failures.txt)

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6)

...clock class: 248 (← default/FREERUN value, never reached 6)

```

• Root Cause: The openshift_ptp_clock_state metric (registered in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/metrics/register.go:57-63 with labels {process, node, iface}) is only set when UpdateClockStateMetrics() in pkg/metrics/exporter.go:15-23 is called with a servo state change for that interface. A metric label combination {node=cnfdf31, iface=ens2f0np0} being entirely absent means linuxptp-daemon on cnfdf31 never processed a servo state log line for ens2f0np0 — i.e., ptp4l never elected that port as SLAVE and never emitted a servo lock event. The explicit role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) in Test 3 for ens2f3np3 corroborates this: both follower ports are stuck in LISTENING/unelected state. The tgm suite failures (clock class 248 = freerun, never 6) indicate the upstream Grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock; with the T-GM in freerun the entire downstream chain — BC → dualfollower slave — cannot lock, which is consistent with all suites failing in the same run. Additionally, the pmc bad command: GET / PARENT_DATA_SET errors in the dualnicbc suite (same run, linuxptp-daemon branch release-5.0) indicate a ptp4l management interface issue. The commit OCPBUGS-90708: Sync from upstream (22-Jun-2026) in linuxptp-daemon (merged 2026-06-23, two days after this run) and the commit OCPBUGS-88369: Fix CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs in cloud-event-proxy (merged 2026-06-25) were both pending at the time of this job.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely pre-dates the fix in linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (OCPBUGS-90708 / CNF-24996, merged 2026-06-23, SHA 0459bc0) and cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (OCPBUGS-88369, merged 2026-06-25, SHA fc5d567) — both merged after this CI run on 2026-06-21. The breaking change introducing the regression is Unknown (upstream/downstream commit not visible in the shallow clone).
• Is it a flake? No — all four test suites in the same job (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) failed with consistent, correlated errors. The T-GM staying at clock class 248 is a systematic failure, not random jitter.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the T-GM node achieves GNSS lock (clock class 6) before running downstream sync tests; also ensure the linuxptp-daemon and cloud-event-proxy images built from release-5.0 include the fixes from OCPBUGS-90708 (pmc/ptp4l management interface fix) and OCPBUGS-88369 (CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs), both of which were merged after this job ran.

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="",

slaveIfs=[ens2f3np3 ens2f0np0]). Per-interface results:

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found

```

```

Broader context from other suites (junit-failures.txt)

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

```

tgm suite (junit-failures.txt)

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6)

...clock class: 248 (← default/FREERUN value, never reached 6)

```

• Root Cause: The openshift_ptp_clock_state metric (registered in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/metrics/register.go:57-63 with labels {process, node, iface}) is only set when UpdateClockStateMetrics() in pkg/metrics/exporter.go:15-23 is called with a servo state change for that interface. A metric label combination {node=cnfdf31, iface=ens2f0np0} being entirely absent means linuxptp-daemon on cnfdf31 never processed a servo state log line for ens2f0np0 — i.e., ptp4l never elected that port as SLAVE and never emitted a servo lock event. The explicit role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) in Test 3 for ens2f3np3 corroborates this: both follower ports are stuck in LISTENING/unelected state. The tgm suite failures (clock class 248 = freerun, never 6) indicate the upstream Grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock; with the T-GM in freerun the entire downstream chain — BC → dualfollower slave — cannot lock, which is consistent with all suites failing in the same run. Additionally, the pmc bad command: GET / PARENT_DATA_SET errors in the dualnicbc suite (same run, linuxptp-daemon branch release-5.0) indicate a ptp4l management interface issue. The commit OCPBUGS-90708: Sync from upstream (22-Jun-2026) in linuxptp-daemon (merged 2026-06-23, two days after this run) and the commit OCPBUGS-88369: Fix CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs in cloud-event-proxy (merged 2026-06-25) were both pending at the time of this job.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely pre-dates the fix in linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (OCPBUGS-90708 / CNF-24996, merged 2026-06-23, SHA 0459bc0) and cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (OCPBUGS-88369, merged 2026-06-25, SHA fc5d567) — both merged after this CI run on 2026-06-21. The breaking change introducing the regression is Unknown (upstream/downstream commit not visible in the shallow clone).
• Is it a flake? No — all four test suites in the same job (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) failed with consistent, correlated errors. The T-GM staying at clock class 248 is a systematic failure, not random jitter.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the T-GM node achieves GNSS lock (clock class 6) before running downstream sync tests; also ensure the linuxptp-daemon and cloud-event-proxy images built from release-5.0 include the fixes from OCPBUGS-90708 (pmc/ptp4l management interface fix) and OCPBUGS-88369 (CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs), both of which were merged after this job ran.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 9 failures stem from two independent root causes: pmc being invoked with split arguments causing PARENT_DATA_SET queries to return "bad command" errors, and the BC node's ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) due to an unlocked upstream GM — with event-framework consumer timeouts as a downstream consequence.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: PMC "bad command" for PARENT_DATA_SET (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: The pmc tool is being invoked with "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as two separate argv elements rather than as the single combined string "GET PARENT_DATA_SET". In non-interactive (batch) mode, linuxptp's pmc.c calls do_command(argv[optind]) for each remaining argv item; processing "GET" alone yields "bad command: GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone yields "bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET". Other pmc commands (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET used by the clock-class test) still work, confirming ptp4l itself is up and the socket is reachable — only the argument quoting for PARENT_DATA_SET queries is broken. The new non-interactive helper RunPMCGetParentDS in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 passes the full "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string as one exec.Command arg (which should be fine via sscanf tokenizing). The split-arg pattern strongly implicates the test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test calling pmc ... GET PARENT_DATA_SET without quoting, or a behavior change in the RHEL 10 linuxptp pmc binary that now treats the space-separated arg as two tokens.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0 — "upstream-sync-2026-06-22", merged 2026-06-22) which synced upstream linuxptp changes into release-5.0; the pmc binary on RHEL 10 / RHCOS 10.2 may have changed its batch-mode argument-parsing behaviour. Test code path: /tmp/cnf-C4K0w/ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (not cloned, exact commit unknown).
• Is it a flake? No — identical error appears verbatim across dualnicbc AND dualnicbcha suites in the same run, showing systematic breakage.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure pmc is invoked with the action and management-ID as a single quoted argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configPath, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") in Go, or pmc ... "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" in shell). Alternatively, switch all GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to the interactive expect-based RunPMCExpGetParentDS (linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:132) which uses e.Send("GET PARENT_DATA_SET\n") and is known to work.

• Group 2: BC ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "PTP metric is present verifies on slave", "The slave node network interface is taken down and up", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published ... cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString>: incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Cross-corroborating evidence from tgm suite (same CI run):

```

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6) ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM, Expected : false to be true

```

• Root Cause: The WPC Grandmaster node (tgm) itself is not reaching LOCKED state (clock class 6) — demonstrated by multiple tgm suite failures in the same CI run reporting clock class never reaches 6. With the GM in FREERUN/HOLDOVER (class 248), the BC node (cnfdf32, running ptpconfig test-bc-master1 against ptp4l.1.config) cannot lock its upstream port ens2f0np0, causing ptp4l to report class 248. After the network-outage test brings ens2f0np0 down and up, ptp4l without a valid upstream GM elects itself MASTER on that port instead of returning to SLAVE. PTP time-sync metrics (openshift_ptp_clock_state, openshift_ptp_offset_ns) are absent because the linuxptp-daemon does not emit offset/clock-state metrics when not locked; CNE event metrics (cne_api_events_published) are present showing cloud-event-proxy is running but the PTP layer is FREERUN.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — tgm (WPC GNSS/GM hardware) failures point to either a hardware/environment issue on the telco5g lab testbed or a change in the GM node's configuration/firmware. The linuxptp-daemon upstream sync PR #613 (0459bc0, 2026-06-22) is a candidate if it changed ts2phc or WPC GM handling.
• Is it a flake? No — 4 separate tests in dualnicbc plus parallel tests and matching tgm failures all confirm systemic FREERUN state.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate and restore the WPC GM node's GNSS/GPS signal lock (tgm hardware/config), or check whether PR #613's upstream sync changed ts2phc GM behaviour. Once the GM reaches class 6, all BC and slave downstream clock-class/metric/outage-recovery tests should pass.

• Group 3: Cloud-event-proxy PushInitialValue timeout (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "PTP Slave Clock Sync" [parallel])
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The consumer pod in ptp-event-framework-test never logs "Got CurrentState: ({.*})", meaning it does not receive an initial state push from the cloud-event-proxy sidecar after the linuxptp-daemon pod restart. The most recent cloud-event-proxy commit is fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime" (PR #701). If this PR changed how dual-NIC BC events are published (e.g., restructuring which publisher emits SyncStateChange for TBC profiles — see cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:388-393), the initial-state push path PushInitialValue may no longer fire on daemon restart for this BC topology. An alternative explanation is that with ptp4l in FREERUN (Group 2), no LOCKED→FREERUN state transition occurs at restart, so no event is generated to push.
• Breaking PR/Commit: cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime"), merged just before this CI run. Reference: cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:375-393 and metrics/tbc_test.go.
• Is it a flake? No — same timeou


TL;DR: WPC T-GM grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock (class 248), collapsing all 4 suites; pmc argument bug added 5 independent failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 20/25 failures — GM in FREERUN (clock class 248), cascading to all BC/slave/follower sync tests

Affects: tgm (5/5), dualnicbcha (~6/8), dualnicbc (~6/9), dualfollower (3/3). The WPC T-GM node hosting linuxptp-daemon-7g7z8 never transitioned out of FREERUN during the run. With no locked GM advertising Announce messages, the entire downstream chain — BC → dualnicbc → dualnicbcha → dualfollower slaves — could not lock. The tgm log stream stayed open but hit context deadline exceeded after 340 s without ever emitting a LOCKED event; all four state-based tgm tests timed out on Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM / : false. The dualfollower node cnfdf31 exhibits both missing openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 and ens2f3np3 stuck in LISTENING — consistent with no upstream Announce to trigger SLAVE election.


• 5/25 failures — pmc invoked with split arguments; GET PARENT_DATA_SET rejected as two bad commands

Affects: dualnicbc ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and dualnicbcha ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master"). pmc is called with GET and PARENT_DATA_SET as separate argv elements; the binary responds bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. Identical verbatim error appears in both suites, ruling out a flake. Likely triggered by the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary (linuxptp ≥ 4.3, el10_2) changing batch-mode argument tokenization, or the test helper failing to quote the combined string. Other pmc queries (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET) still succeed, confirming the socket and ptp4l process are reachable.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN / GNSS never lockedAll 3~6~6All 5
pmc split-arg bug—32—

• The GM FREERUN failure is shared across all 4 suites — it is the single largest driver and the only failure in tgm and dualfollower.
• The pmc split-arg bug is shared between dualnicbc and dualnicbcha only (suites that exercise PARENT_DATA_SET queries via the BC node).
• No failures are genuinely suite-specific; the dualfollower and tgm failures are pure downstream consequences of the shared GM not locking.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job and inspect GM GNSS hardware first. Confirm whether the WPC T-GM node achieves GNSS/DPLL lock in a fresh run. If it fails again, check the GNSS antenna cable, receiver status, and ts2phc DPLL netlink events on that node. This single fix would resolve ~20/25 failures.

2. Fix pmc invocation to pass GET PARENT_DATA_SET as a single quoted argument. In both the test helper (ptp-operator-conformance-test) and any exec.Command / shell call in linuxptp-daemon, ensure the action+management-ID are passed as one argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET")), or switch to the interactive RunPMCExpGetParentDS path with lowercase command ("get PARENT_DATA_SET") to match the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary's expected input. This resolves the remaining 5 failures.

3. Add a pre-flight GM-lock gate to the CI job. Before running any BC/slave/follower suite, assert that the T-GM node has clock class ≤ 7 (LOCKED); fail fast with a clear infra error rather than letting all 4 suites time out. This would surface the GNSS issue immediately and save ~30 min of wasted CI time per run.


Overall Issue Class: test_flake (dominant: GNSS hardware failure is a known lab environmental flake) + test_regression (secondary: pmc argument bug introduced with RHCOS 10.2 / linuxptp upstream sync 0459bc0)

Affects: dualnicbc ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority") and dualnicbcha ("Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master"). pmc is called with GET and PARENT_DATA_SET as separate argv elements; the binary responds bad command: GET / bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET. Identical verbatim error appears in both suites, ruling out a flake. Likely triggered by the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary (linuxptp ≥ 4.3, el10_2) changing batch-mode argument tokenization, or the test helper failing to quote the combined string. Other pmc queries (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET) still succeed, confirming the socket and ptp4l process are reachable.



Cross-Suite Patterns:


Root Causedualfollowerdualnicbcdualnicbchatgm
GM FREERUN / GNSS never lockedAll 3~6~6All 5
pmc split-arg bug—32—

• The GM FREERUN failure is shared across all 4 suites — it is the single largest driver and the only failure in tgm and dualfollower.
• The pmc split-arg bug is shared between dualnicbc and dualnicbcha only (suites that exercise PARENT_DATA_SET queries via the BC node).
• No failures are genuinely suite-specific; the dualfollower and tgm failures are pure downstream consequences of the shared GM not locking.


Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job and inspect GM GNSS hardware first. Confirm whether the WPC T-GM node achieves GNSS/DPLL lock in a fresh run. If it fails again, check the GNSS antenna cable, receiver status, and ts2phc DPLL netlink events on that node. This single fix would resolve ~20/25 failures.

2. Fix pmc invocation to pass GET PARENT_DATA_SET as a single quoted argument. In both the test helper (ptp-operator-conformance-test) and any exec.Command / shell call in linuxptp-daemon, ensure the action+management-ID are passed as one argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", ..., "GET PARENT_DATA_SET")), or switch to the interactive RunPMCExpGetParentDS path with lowercase command ("get PARENT_DATA_SET") to match the RHCOS 10.2 pmc binary's expected input. This resolves the remaining 5 failures.

3. Add a pre-flight GM-lock gate to the CI job. Before running any BC/slave/follower suite, assert that the T-GM node has clock class ≤ 7 (LOCKED); fail fast with a clear infra error rather than letting all 4 suites time out. This would surface the GNSS issue immediately and save ~30 min of wasted CI time per run.


Overall Issue Class: test_flake (dominant: GNSS hardware failure is a known lab environmental flake) + test_regression (secondary: pmc argument bug introduced with RHCOS 10.2 / linuxptp upstream sync 0459bc0)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — 25/25 failures, 4/4 suites completely down in a nightly periodic job.




Per-Suite Details



dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 dualfollower ClockSync tests timed out waiting for node cnfdf31's follower interfaces to reach LOCKED state because the openshift_ptp_clock_state metric for ens2f0np0 was never emitted by linuxptp-daemon, and ens2f3np3 was stuck in LISTENING rather than SLAVE role.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Slave node never locked — missing clock_state metric and port stuck in LISTENING (affects: all 3 tests)
• Evidence:

```

Tests 1 & 2 — identical error

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig test-slave1

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="ptp/clock-under-test",

slaveIfs=[ens2f0np0 ens2f3np3]). Per-interface results:

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found,

available op[tions: ...]

```

```

Test 3 — additional symptom

no Follower port in expected LOCKED state for ptpconfig temp

(node=cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, label="",

slaveIfs=[ens2f3np3 ens2f0np0]). Per-interface results:

ens2f3np3: role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING)

ens2f0np0: clock state metric error: metric: openshift_ptp_clock_state,

nodeName: cnfdf31.telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com, aIf: ens2f0np0 not found

```

```

Broader context from other suites (junit-failures.txt)

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config:

bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

```

tgm suite (junit-failures.txt)

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6)

...clock class: 248 (← default/FREERUN value, never reached 6)

```

• Root Cause: The openshift_ptp_clock_state metric (registered in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/metrics/register.go:57-63 with labels {process, node, iface}) is only set when UpdateClockStateMetrics() in pkg/metrics/exporter.go:15-23 is called with a servo state change for that interface. A metric label combination {node=cnfdf31, iface=ens2f0np0} being entirely absent means linuxptp-daemon on cnfdf31 never processed a servo state log line for ens2f0np0 — i.e., ptp4l never elected that port as SLAVE and never emitted a servo lock event. The explicit role mismatch (expected=SLAVE, got=LISTENING) in Test 3 for ens2f3np3 corroborates this: both follower ports are stuck in LISTENING/unelected state. The tgm suite failures (clock class 248 = freerun, never 6) indicate the upstream Grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock; with the T-GM in freerun the entire downstream chain — BC → dualfollower slave — cannot lock, which is consistent with all suites failing in the same run. Additionally, the pmc bad command: GET / PARENT_DATA_SET errors in the dualnicbc suite (same run, linuxptp-daemon branch release-5.0) indicate a ptp4l management interface issue. The commit OCPBUGS-90708: Sync from upstream (22-Jun-2026) in linuxptp-daemon (merged 2026-06-23, two days after this run) and the commit OCPBUGS-88369: Fix CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs in cloud-event-proxy (merged 2026-06-25) were both pending at the time of this job.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely pre-dates the fix in linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (OCPBUGS-90708 / CNF-24996, merged 2026-06-23, SHA 0459bc0) and cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (OCPBUGS-88369, merged 2026-06-25, SHA fc5d567) — both merged after this CI run on 2026-06-21. The breaking change introducing the regression is Unknown (upstream/downstream commit not visible in the shallow clone).
• Is it a flake? No — all four test suites in the same job (dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, tgm) failed with consistent, correlated errors. The T-GM staying at clock class 248 is a systematic failure, not random jitter.
• Suggested Fix: Verify the T-GM node achieves GNSS lock (clock class 6) before running downstream sync tests; also ensure the linuxptp-daemon and cloud-event-proxy images built from release-5.0 include the fixes from OCPBUGS-90708 (pmc/ptp4l management interface fix) and OCPBUGS-88369 (CLOCK_REALTIME dual-publisher conflict in ParseTBCLogs), both of which were merged after this job ran.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (9 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 9 failures stem from two independent root causes: pmc being invoked with split arguments causing PARENT_DATA_SET queries to return "bad command" errors, and the BC node's ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) due to an unlocked upstream GM — with event-framework consumer timeouts as a downstream consequence.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: PMC "bad command" for PARENT_DATA_SET (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

parentPortIdentity.clockIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

and

```

grandmasterIdentity not found in pmc output for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config: bad command: GET

bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET

```

• Root Cause: The pmc tool is being invoked with "GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" as two separate argv elements rather than as the single combined string "GET PARENT_DATA_SET". In non-interactive (batch) mode, linuxptp's pmc.c calls do_command(argv[optind]) for each remaining argv item; processing "GET" alone yields "bad command: GET" and "PARENT_DATA_SET" alone yields "bad command: PARENT_DATA_SET". Other pmc commands (e.g. GET DEFAULT_DATA_SET used by the clock-class test) still work, confirming ptp4l itself is up and the socket is reachable — only the argument quoting for PARENT_DATA_SET queries is broken. The new non-interactive helper RunPMCGetParentDS in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:294 passes the full "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" string as one exec.Command arg (which should be fine via sscanf tokenizing). The split-arg pattern strongly implicates the test helper in ptp-operator-conformance-test calling pmc ... GET PARENT_DATA_SET without quoting, or a behavior change in the RHEL 10 linuxptp pmc binary that now treats the space-separated arg as two tokens.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Likely linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0 — "upstream-sync-2026-06-22", merged 2026-06-22) which synced upstream linuxptp changes into release-5.0; the pmc binary on RHEL 10 / RHCOS 10.2 may have changed its batch-mode argument-parsing behaviour. Test code path: /tmp/cnf-C4K0w/ptp-operator-conformance-test/test/conformance/serial/ptp.go (not cloned, exact commit unknown).
• Is it a flake? No — identical error appears verbatim across dualnicbc AND dualnicbcha suites in the same run, showing systematic breakage.
• Suggested Fix: Ensure pmc is invoked with the action and management-ID as a single quoted argument string (e.g. exec.Command("pmc", "-u", "-b", "0", "-f", configPath, "GET PARENT_DATA_SET") in Go, or pmc ... "GET PARENT_DATA_SET" in shell). Alternatively, switch all GET PARENT_DATA_SET queries to the interactive expect-based RunPMCExpGetParentDS (linuxptp-daemon/pkg/pmc/pmc.go:132) which uses e.Send("GET PARENT_DATA_SET\n") and is known to work.

• Group 2: BC ptp4l stuck in FREERUN (clock class 248) (affects: "Verify clockClass when locking PTP source on dual NIC boundary clock", "PTP metric is present verifies on slave", "The slave node network interface is taken down and up", "BC clock class recovers to Locked after upstream link outage")
• Evidence:

```

Expected PMC clock class 6 for /var/run/ptp4l.1.config

Expected : 248 to equal : 6

```

```

Time metrics are not detected

Expected : # HELP cne_api_events_published ... cne_api_events_published{address="/sync/ptp-status/clock-class",status="success"} 2

```

```

ens2f0np0 should recover to SLAVE

Expected <*errors.errorString>: incorrect role for ens2f0np0, role expected=1(SLAVE), role observed=2(MASTER)

```

```

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM

Expected : false to be true

```

Cross-corroborating evidence from tgm suite (same CI run):

```

Expected ptp4l clock class state to eventually be Locked (class 6) ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

Expected ptp4l clock class to eventually be 6 for GM, Expected : false to be true

```

• Root Cause: The WPC Grandmaster node (tgm) itself is not reaching LOCKED state (clock class 6) — demonstrated by multiple tgm suite failures in the same CI run reporting clock class never reaches 6. With the GM in FREERUN/HOLDOVER (class 248), the BC node (cnfdf32, running ptpconfig test-bc-master1 against ptp4l.1.config) cannot lock its upstream port ens2f0np0, causing ptp4l to report class 248. After the network-outage test brings ens2f0np0 down and up, ptp4l without a valid upstream GM elects itself MASTER on that port instead of returning to SLAVE. PTP time-sync metrics (openshift_ptp_clock_state, openshift_ptp_offset_ns) are absent because the linuxptp-daemon does not emit offset/clock-state metrics when not locked; CNE event metrics (cne_api_events_published) are present showing cloud-event-proxy is running but the PTP layer is FREERUN.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — tgm (WPC GNSS/GM hardware) failures point to either a hardware/environment issue on the telco5g lab testbed or a change in the GM node's configuration/firmware. The linuxptp-daemon upstream sync PR #613 (0459bc0, 2026-06-22) is a candidate if it changed ts2phc or WPC GM handling.
• Is it a flake? No — 4 separate tests in dualnicbc plus parallel tests and matching tgm failures all confirm systemic FREERUN state.
• Suggested Fix: Investigate and restore the WPC GM node's GNSS/GPS signal lock (tgm hardware/config), or check whether PR #613's upstream sync changed ts2phc GM behaviour. Once the GM reaches class 6, all BC and slave downstream clock-class/metric/outage-recovery tests should pass.

• Group 3: Cloud-event-proxy PushInitialValue timeout (affects: "Should receive events after linuxptp-daemon pod restart", "PTP Slave Clock Sync" [parallel])
• Evidence:

```

timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

```

could not push initial event, err=timedout PushInitialValue, waiting for log in ns=ptp-event-framework-test pod=consumer, looking for = Got CurrentState: ({.*})

```

• Root Cause: The consumer pod in ptp-event-framework-test never logs "Got CurrentState: ({.*})", meaning it does not receive an initial state push from the cloud-event-proxy sidecar after the linuxptp-daemon pod restart. The most recent cloud-event-proxy commit is fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime" (PR #701). If this PR changed how dual-NIC BC events are published (e.g., restructuring which publisher emits SyncStateChange for TBC profiles — see cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:388-393), the initial-state push path PushInitialValue may no longer fire on daemon restart for this BC topology. An alternative explanation is that with ptp4l in FREERUN (Group 2), no LOCKED→FREERUN state transition occurs at restart, so no event is generated to push.
• Breaking PR/Commit: cloud-event-proxy PR #701 (fc5d567 — "fix-tbc-dual-publisher-clock-realtime"), merged just before this CI run. Reference: cloud-event-proxy/plugins/ptp_operator/metrics/manager.go:375-393 and metrics/tbc_test.go.
• Is it a flake? No — same timeou


TL;DR: WPC T-GM grandmaster never achieved GNSS lock (class 248), collapsing all 4 suites; pmc argument bug added 5 independent failures.

With no locked GM advertising Announce messages, the entire downstream chain — BC → dualnicbc → dualnicbcha → dualfollower slaves — could not lock.
